<p>The <b>2012–13 Scottish Premier League</b> was the fifteenth and final season of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a>, the highest division of <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Scotland" title="Football in Scotland">Scottish football</a>, since its inception in 1998. The season began on 4 August 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and ended on 19 May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Twelve teams contested the league. <a href="/wiki/Ross_County_F.C." title="Ross County F.C.">Ross County</a> (champions) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dundee_FC" title="Dundee FC">Dundee</a> (runners-up) were promoted from the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Scottish_First_Division" title="2011–12 Scottish First Division">2011–12 First Division</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Dunfermline_Athletic_F.C." title="Dunfermline Athletic F.C.">Dunfermline</a> (relegated) and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>, which was liquidated and whose successor company was denied permission to take its place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Dundee took its place, while the successor was eventually granted the old company's membership to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a> and admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_League_Third_Division" title="Scottish Football League Third Division">Scottish Football League Third Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 April, Celtic retained their title after a 4–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/Inverness_Caledonian_Thistle_F.C." title="Inverness Caledonian Thistle F.C.">Inverness Caledonian Thistle</a> at <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>This was the final season of the Scottish Premier League before it was abolished in June 2013, when the SPL and SFL merged to form the new <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Professional_Football_League" title="Scottish Professional Football League">Scottish Professional Football League</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> with its top division being known as the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premiership" title="Scottish Premiership">Scottish Premiership</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotland_location_map.svg" title="File:Scotland location map.svg"></a></div>
Location of teams in <b>Scottish Premier League 2012–13</b></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dunfermline_Athletic_F.C." title="Dunfermline Athletic F.C.">Dunfermline</a> were relegated from the 2011–12 Scottish Premier League. <a href="/wiki/Ross_County_F.C." title="Ross County F.C.">Ross County</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Scottish_First_Division" title="2011–12 Scottish First Division">2011–12 Scottish First Division</a>, were promoted. The 2012–13 season marks the top-flight debut for the Highland team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The participation of <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>, who failed to exit <a href="/wiki/Administration_(British_football)" title="Administration (British football)">administration</a> via a CVA after a proposed agreement with its creditors was rejected, was dependent on the outcome of a vote by SPL clubs on whether or not Rangers would be able to transfer their SPL membership share to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Rangers_Football_Club_Ltd" title="The Rangers Football Club Ltd">new company</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-club_12_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-club_12-12">[12]</a></sup> When the fixture list was published on 18 June 2012, Rangers were replaced by the term "Club 12", pending the outcome of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-club_12_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-club_12-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Eight clubs publicly declared that they would oppose the membership transfer to Rangers' newco, which would mean that they could not play in the SPL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The vote took place on 4 July 2012, and Rangers were refused re-entry to the SPL by a 10-1 majority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vote_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vote-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dundee_F.C." title="Dundee F.C.">Dundee</a>, who had finished second in the 2011–12 Scottish First Division, were invited to replace Rangers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vote_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vote-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>

Rules for classification: 1) points; 2) goal difference; 3) number of goals scored<br/>
<sup>1</sup> Since the winners of <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Scottish_Cup" title="2012–13 Scottish Cup">2012–13 Scottish Cup</a>, Celtic are already qualified to <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">2013–14 UEFA Champions League</a>, the runners–up Hibernian secured a spot in 2013–14 UEFA Europa League in the second qualifying round.<br/>
<sup>2</sup> Teams in the bottom half at the time of the split may not overtake a team in the top 6 at the time of the split.<br/>
<b>(C)</b> = Champion; <b>(R)</b> = Relegated; <b>(P)</b> = Promoted; <b>(E)</b> = Eliminated; <b>(O)</b> = Play-off winner; <b>(A)</b> = Advances to a further round.<br/>
Only applicable when the season is not finished:<br/>
<b>(Q)</b> = Qualified to the phase of tournament indicated; <b>(TQ)</b> = Qualified to tournament, but not yet to the particular phase indicated; <b>(RQ)</b> = Qualified to the relegation tournament indicated; <b>(DQ)</b> = Disqualified from tournament.<br/></small></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Matches_34.E2.80.9338">Matches 34–38</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Scottish_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Matches 34–38">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After 33 matches, the league splits into two sections of six teams each, with teams playing every other team in their section once (either at home or away). The exact matches are determined upon the league table at the time of the split.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scoring">Scoring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Scottish_Premier_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Scoring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>First goal of the season: <a href="/wiki/Kris_Commons" title="Kris Commons">Kris Commons</a> for Celtic against <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a> (<small><i>4 August 2012</i></small>)</li>
<li>Fastest goal of the season: <b>12 seconds</b>, <a href="/wiki/Kris_Commons" title="Kris Commons">Kris Commons</a> for <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> against <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a> (<small><i>16 March 2013</i></small>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>Latest goal of the season: <b>94 minutes</b>, <a href="/wiki/Georgios_Samaras" title="Georgios Samaras">Georgios Samaras</a> for <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> against <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a> (<small><i>16 March 2013</i></small>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>Largest winning margin: <b>5 goals</b>
<ul>
<li>St Mirren 0–5 Celtic (<small><i>20 October 2012</i></small>)</li>
<li>Celtic 5–0 Dundee (<small><i>24 February 2013</i></small>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Highest scoring game: <b>9 goals</b>
<ul>
<li>St Mirren 5–4 Ross County (<small><i>29 September 2012</i></small>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Most goals scored in a match by a single team: <b>6 goals</b>
<ul>
<li>Celtic 6–2 Dundee United (<small><i>16 February 2013</i></small>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Most goals scored in a match by a losing team: <b>4 goals</b>
<ul>
<li>St Mirren 5–4 Ross County (<small><i>29 September 2012</i></small>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
